52	# MEG/EEG are INPUT-ONLY (never targets) — encoder embedding only, no decoder.
53	# ``type: seq_token`` keeps the input masking on the image_mask path (see
54	# PresenceAwareUnifiedMasking); its autoregressive decoder branch is never reached
55	# because neural mods stay out of out_domains. See notes/4m_neural_modality_design.md.
56	_NEURAL_MODALITY_INFO = {
57	    "tok_meg": {
58	        "vocab_size": MEG_VOCAB_SIZE,
59	        "encoder_embedding": partial(
60	            MegEncoderEmbedding,
61	            vocab_size=MEG_VOCAB_SIZE,
62	            n_rvq=MEG_N_RVQ,
63	            n_sources=MEG_N_SOURCES,
64	            n_time=MEG_N_TIME,
65	        ),
66	        "min_tokens": 0,
67	        "max_tokens": MEG_POSITIONS_PER_TRIAL,  # 128 grid cells (RVQ summed per cell)
68	        "type": "seq_token",
69	        "id": generate_uint15_hash("tok_meg"),
70	        "path": "tok_meg",
71	        "pretokenized": True,
72	    },
73	    "tok_eeg": {

79	            padding_idx=None,  # code 0 is a real LaBraM code; absence is presence-masked
80	        ),

97	    },

100	# MEG/EEG OUTPUT (target) modalities — predicted as a reconstruction regularizer.
101	# They use ``type: neural_grid`` so 4M routes them through the PARALLEL decoder branch
102	# (not seq_token's autoregressive path) and the trainer's square ``max_tokens`` rule for
103	# ``img`` leaves their non-square grids alone. Each reads an existing on-disk folder via
104	# ``path`` (no repack); the rename seam splits one sampled trial into these heads.
105	# MEG: one head per RVQ layer (layer-specific 512-vocab codebooks) over the 16x8 grid.
106	for _q, _meg_mod in enumerate(MEG_RVQ_OUT_MODALITIES):
107	    _NEURAL_MODALITY_INFO[_meg_mod] = {
108	        "vocab_size": MEG_VOCAB_SIZE,
109	        "encoder_embedding": None,  # output-only
110	        "decoder_embedding": partial(
111	            MegRVQDecoderEmbedding,

113	            n_sources=MEG_N_SOURCES,
114	            n_time=MEG_N_TIME,
115	        ),
116	        "min_tokens": 0,
117	        "max_tokens": MEG_POSITIONS_PER_TRIAL,  # 128 grid cells
118	        "type": NEURAL_GRID_TYPE,
119	        "id": generate_uint15_hash(_meg_mod),
120	        "path": MEG_OUT_SOURCE_PATH,  # all four read the tok_meg folder
121	        "pretokenized": True,
122	    }
123	# EEG: a single codebook -> one head over the 17-token sequence.
124	_NEURAL_MODALITY_INFO[EEG_OUT_MODALITY] = {
125	    "vocab_size": EEG_VOCAB_SIZE,
126	    "encoder_embedding": None,  # output-only
127	    "decoder_embedding": partial(
128	        EegDecoderEmbedding,
129	        vocab_size=EEG_VOCAB_SIZE,

135	    "id": generate_uint15_hash(EEG_OUT_MODALITY),
136	    "path": EEG_OUT_SOURCE_PATH,  # reads the tok_eeg folder
137	    "pretokenized": True,
138	}

140	_REGISTERED_TRAINING: bool | None = None
141	
142	
143	def register(training: bool = True) -> None:
144	    """Inject MEG/EEG modalities into 4M's global registries.
145	
146	    Always updates ``MODALITY_TRANSFORMS`` for tok_meg/tok_eeg so train vs val
147	    trial sampling can be switched by calling ``register(training=False)``.
148	    """
149	    global _REGISTERED_TRAINING
150	
151	    for name, info in _NEURAL_MODALITY_INFO.items():
152	        _mi.MODALITY_INFO.setdefault(name, info)
153	
154	    # THINGS on-disk folders use tok_rgb / tok_depth; stock 4M registers @224 names.
155	    for alias, src in (("tok_rgb", "tok_rgb@224"), ("tok_depth", "tok_depth@224")):
156	        if alias not in _mi.MODALITY_INFO and src in _mi.MODALITY_INFO:
157	            info = copy.deepcopy(_mi.MODALITY_INFO[src])
158	            info["path"] = alias
159	            _mi.MODALITY_INFO[alias] = info
160	
161	    # THINGS vision shards are flat (196,) with no augmentation axis; stock
162	    # TokTransform would index that axis and collapse the grid to one token.
163	    # ThingsTokTransform falls back to stock behaviour for (n_augs, n_tokens),
164	    # so the shared "tok_rgb" transform key stays correct for CC12M too.
165	    for vision_mod in ("tok_rgb", "tok_depth"):
166	        _mi.MODALITY_TRANSFORMS[vision_mod] = ThingsTokTransform()
167	
168	    _mi.MODALITY_TRANSFORMS["tok_meg"] = MegTokTransform(training=training)
169	    _mi.MODALITY_TRANSFORMS["tok_eeg"] = EegTokTransform(training=training)
170	    _mi.MODALITY_TRANSFORMS.setdefault("meg_mask", MaskFlagTransform())
171	    _mi.MODALITY_TRANSFORMS.setdefault("eeg_mask", MaskFlagTransform())
172	
173	    # OUTPUT modalities: the trial pick + RVQ split already happened in the rename seam,
174	    # so these transforms just clip to the head's vocab. (Training-mode trial sampling for
175	    # the split is configured on NeuralTargetSplitter, not here.)
176	    for meg_mod in MEG_RVQ_OUT_MODALITIES:
177	        _mi.MODALITY_TRANSFORMS[meg_mod] = NeuralTargetTransform(code_max=MEG_CODE_MAX)
178	    _mi.MODALITY_TRANSFORMS[EEG_OUT_MODALITY] = NeuralTargetTransform(code_max=EEG_CODE_MAX)
179	    _REGISTERED_TRAINING = training
180	
181	
182	register()

Tool reply2026-05-28T02:00:50.695Z
1	"""Generalized trial-sampling for stacked neural token arrays (MEG / EEG).
2	
3	Each ``tok_meg/<image_id>.npy`` or ``tok_eeg/<image_id>.npy`` stores::
4	
5	    arr.shape == (n_trials, *trial_shape)   # int16
6	
7	For images lacking neural data, the packer writes a sentinel::
8	
9	    np.full((1, *trial_shape), NEURAL_SENTINEL_VALUE, dtype=np.int16)
10	
11	Pure-Python; only depends on numpy.
12	"""
13	
14	from __future__ import annotations
15	
16	import numpy as np
17	
18	from neural_constants import (
19	    EEG_OUT_MODALITY,
20	    EEG_TRIAL_SHAPE,
21	    EEG_TOKENS_PER_TRIAL,
22	    MEG_GRID_SHAPE,
23	    MEG_RVQ_OUT_MODALITIES,
24	    MEG_TRIAL_SHAPE,
25	    MEG_TOKENS_PER_TRIAL,
26	    NEURAL_PLACEHOLDER_CODE,
27	    NEURAL_SENTINEL_VALUE,
28	)
29	
30	# Backward-compatible aliases (prefer neural_constants in new code).
31	SENTINEL_VALUE: int = NEURAL_SENTINEL_VALUE
32	PLACEHOLDER_FILL_VALUE: int = NEURAL_PLACEHOLDER_CODE
33	
34	
35	def is_placeholder(arr: np.ndarray, trial_shape: tuple[int, ...]) -> bool:
36	    """Detect sentinel pattern: shape ``(1, *trial_shape)`` filled with -1."""
37	    expected = (1, *trial_shape)
38	    return bool(
39	        arr.ndim == len(expected)
40	        and tuple(arr.shape) == expected
41	        and (arr == NEURAL_SENTINEL_VALUE).all()
42	    )
43	
44	
45	class NeuralTrialSampleTransform:
46	    """Pick one trial per call and reshape it to a 4M-ready token array.
47	
48	    The picked trial (``trial_shape``) is reshaped to ``out_shape`` — same element
49	    count, but laid out the way the encoder embedding expects. MEG keeps its RVQ
50	    axis (``(128, 4)``) so the embedding can sum residual codebooks per cell; EEG
51	    stays a flat ``(17,)`` sequence. See ``notes/4m_neural_modality_design.md``.
52	
53	    Args:
54	        trial_shape: On-disk inner shape per trial (e.g. ``MEG_TRIAL_SHAPE``).
55	        out_shape: Reshaped per-trial output. Defaults to flat ``(prod(trial_shape),)``.
56	        training: If True, sample a uniform random trial; if False, always trial 0.
57	        seed: Optional RNG seed for reproducibility within one transform instance.
58	    """
59	
60	    def __init__(
61	        self,
62	        trial_shape: tuple[int, ...],
63	        out_shape: tuple[int, ...] | None = None,
64	        training: bool = True,
65	        seed: int | None = None,
66	    ):
67	        self.trial_shape = trial_shape
68	        self.tokens_per_trial = int(np.prod(trial_shape))
69	        self.out_shape = out_shape or (self.tokens_per_trial,)
70	        if int(np.prod(self.out_shape)) != self.tokens_per_trial:
71	            raise ValueError(
72	                f"out_shape {self.out_shape} has a different element count than "
73	                f"trial_shape {trial_shape}"
74	            )
75	        self.training = training
76	        self.rng = np.random.default_rng(seed)
77	
78	    def __call__(self, arr: np.ndarray) -> tuple[np.ndarray, bool]:
79	        ndim = 1 + len(self.trial_shape)
80	        if arr.ndim != ndim or tuple(arr.shape[1:]) != self.trial_shape:
81	            raise ValueError(
82	                f"Trial array must have shape (n_trials, {self.trial_shape}); "
83	                f"got {arr.shape}"
84	            )
85	
86	        if is_placeholder(arr, self.trial_shape):
87	            tokens = np.full(self.out_shape, NEURAL_PLACEHOLDER_CODE, dtype=np.int32)
88	            return tokens, False
89	
90	        n_trials = arr.shape[0]
91	        idx = int(self.rng.integers(0, n_trials)) if self.training else 0
92	        tokens = arr[idx].astype(np.int32).reshape(self.out_shape)
93	        np.clip(tokens, 0, None, out=tokens)
94	        return tokens, True
95	
96	
97	class MegTrialSampleTransform(NeuralTrialSampleTransform):
98	    """MEG trial sampler: ``(n_trials, 16, 8, 4)`` -> ``(128, 4)`` (cells x RVQ layers)."""
99	
100	    def __init__(self, training: bool = True, seed: int | None = None):
101	        super().__init__(
102	            trial_shape=MEG_TRIAL_SHAPE,
103	            out_shape=MEG_GRID_SHAPE,
104	            training=training,
105	            seed=seed,
106	        )
107	
108	
109	class EegTrialSampleTransform(NeuralTrialSampleTransform):
110	    """EEG trial sampler: ``(n_trials, 17)`` -> ``(17,)`` (flat 1D sequence)."""
111	
112	    def __init__(self, training: bool = True, seed: int | None = None):
113	        super().__init__(trial_shape=EEG_TRIAL_SHAPE, training=training, seed=seed)
114	
115	
116	class NeuralTargetSplitter:
117	    """Materialize neural OUTPUT heads from one shared trial, in-place on a sample dict.
118	
119	    The dataloader's ``rename_modalities`` step fans the on-disk ``tok_meg`` / ``tok_eeg``
120	    folder out to every output modality that reads it, so all four ``tok_meg_rvq*`` keys
121	    initially **alias the same** ``(n_trials, 16, 8, 4)`` array. This splitter picks **one**
122	    trial for that array and slices it into the four per-RVQ-layer ``(128,)`` targets — so
123	    the four MEG heads always describe the *same* MEG token. EEG (single codebook) is a
124	    single ``(17,)`` head. Absent (sentinel) data becomes the placeholder code; presence
125	    masking then zeroes its loss. See ``notes/4m_neural_modality_design.md`` §6.
126	
127	    One pick per source per call ⇒ coherent across heads; the picked trial is exactly what
128	    the loss scores, because that single array is both embedded and used as the target ids.
129	    """
130	
131	    def __init__(self, training: bool = True, seed: int | None = None):
132	        self._meg = MegTrialSampleTransform(training=training, seed=seed)
133	        self._eeg = EegTrialSampleTransform(training=training, seed=seed)
134	
135	    def __call__(self, sample: dict) -> dict:
136	        meg_mods = [m for m in MEG_RVQ_OUT_MODALITIES if m in sample]
137	        if meg_mods:
138	            grid, _valid = self._meg(sample[meg_mods[0]])  # (128, n_rvq); one shared pick
139	            for q, mod in enumerate(MEG_RVQ_OUT_MODALITIES):
140	                if mod in sample:
141	                    sample[mod] = np.ascontiguousarray(grid[:, q])
142	        if EEG_OUT_MODALITY in sample:
143	            tokens, _valid = self._eeg(sample[EEG_OUT_MODALITY])  # (17,)
144	            sample[EEG_OUT_MODALITY] = tokens
145	        return sample
146

Now I have a very clear picture. The 4m_training/lib/ folder is a sophisticated wrapper around the stock 4M training pipeline. Let me explain what it does:

  1. train_4m.py: The main entrypoint that:
  2. On import, calls patch_pretrain_utils() from fourm_dataloader.py which patches the stock 4M training loop with neural-aware versions

  3. The run_train function hands off to 4M's run_training_4m.py via runpy.run_path()

  4. fourm_dataloader.py: The "magic glue" — it patches 4M at module level before the training starts:

  5. Replaces UnifiedMasking with a presence-aware version that handles whether neural data exists or is just a sentinel
  6. Swaps in ThingsImageAugmenter for the standard image augmentation to handle THINGS-specific transformations
  7. Intercepts ud.rename_modalities with custom logic that samples individual trials and expands MEG RVQ heads via NeuralTargetSplitter
  8. Overrides the validation dataloader creation to inject neural-aware handling and WDS support

The actual integration happens through monkey-patching 4M's module-level functions before training starts, rather than modifying the training script itself. The fourm_neural_modalities.py file registers MEG/EEG into 4M's modality system at import time, while neural_trial_transform.py contains the core logic for sampling individual trials from stacked arrays and coordinating which trial all MEG RVQ heads use. When the pipeline renames modalities, it also invokes NeuralTargetSplitter.__call__ to handle the neural data splitting. The key sequence is that train_4m.py registers the neural modalities, patches the utility functions, then runs the stock 4M trainer via runpy.run_path(), which builds dataloaders that apply these patched functions—including the modality renaming and neural splitting—within the WDS pipeline.

Looking at lib/train_4m.py, the run_train() function just calls the default 4M training function, so it's not obvious where the neural modality support comes in. The key is that the integration happens through monkey-patching at import time — importing the neural modalities module registers MEG/EEG modalities into 4M's globals, and then patching the pretrain utilities enables the actual data loading and processing. The key insight is that the patching works because runpy.run_path executes the training script in an environment where the fourm module is already loaded in sys.modules with all the replacements applied — so whether the script imports via from statements or module attribute access, it always gets the patched versions since they're baked into the live module objects themselves.

Now I can see the full picture: the integration is real but hidden behind monkey-patching, the trial sampling happens inside the WDS pipeline through the patched function, and this works fine for the main training entrypoint but breaks when run_scaling_experiment_2.py spawns run_training_4m.py as a subprocess since the patches don't carry over to the child process — the scaling experiment would need to either call the training function directly or apply the patches itself in the subprocess.

Now I have a complete picture. Let me explain what's actually happening.

You've misread it — the integration is there, just subtle

The key is at the very top of lib/train_4m.py, before run_train is ever called:

import fourm_neural_modalities   # line 36 — registers MEG/EEG into MODALITY_INFO + MODALITY_TRANSFORMS
patch_pretrain_utils()            # line 47 — monkey-patches 4M's live module objects

By the time run_train calls runpy.run_path("run_training_4m.py"), the fourm package already has four things replaced in-memory:

What's patched Where Effect
ud.UnifiedMasking fourm_dataloader.py:296 PresenceAwareUnifiedMasking zeros loss for absent (sentinel) neural trials
ia.PreTokenizedImageAugmenter fourm_dataloader.py:297 ThingsImageAugmenter handles optional crop_settings
ud.rename_modalities fourm_dataloader.py:299 _rename_modalities, which is where trial sampling happens
pretrain_utils.get_val_dataloader fourm_dataloader.py:310 Adds WDS support for val (solving your earlier question)

The trial sampling path specifically

The WDS pipeline calls rename_modalities on every sample. The patched version _rename_modalities fourm_dataloader.py:83-97 does the stock rename, then immediately calls _NEURAL_SPLITTER(renamed), which is a NeuralTargetSplitter. That splitter (neural_trial_transform.py:116-145):

  1. Sees the on-disk tok_meg array is (n_trials, 16, 8, 4) — multiple stacked trials per image
  2. Picks one trial index (random during train, always trial 0 during eval)
  3. Slices it into the four tok_meg_rvq* output heads — so all four RVQ layers describe the same trial

Images without neural data store a sentinel np.full((1, *shape), -1) (neural_trial_transform.py:35-42), which becomes a placeholder code, and PresenceAwareUnifiedMasking zeros the loss for that sample's neural tokens.

However: this integration does NOT reach run_scaling_experiment_2.py

This is likely the actual gap you're asking about. run_scaling_experiment_2.py launches training via subprocess:

cmd = ["torchrun", ..., "/opt/repo/ml-4m/run_training_4m.py", "--config", ...]
subprocess.run(cmd, ...)

A subprocess starts a fresh Python process. The monkey-patches from patch_pretrain_utils() live only in the current process's memory — they don't cross the subprocess boundary. So when the scaling experiment runs the treatment arm (CONDITION = "rgb_neural"), it will call the unpatched run_training_4m.py, which has no knowledge of MEG/EEG modalities or trial sampling.

To fix this for the treatment arm, run_scaling_experiment_2.py needs to invoke lib/train_4m.py train --config ... instead of calling run_training_4m.py directly:

# current (bypasses patches):
cmd = ["torchrun", "--nproc_per_node=1", "/opt/repo/ml-4m/run_training_4m.py", "--config", ...]

# needed for neural treatment arm:
cmd = ["python", "/opt/repo/4m_training/lib/train_4m.py", "train", "--config", ...]

For the control arm (rgb↔depth only, no neural data), the current subprocess call to run_training_4m.py is fine.

## Verification
+
---

## Route Both Arms Through `lib/train_4m.py`

### Context
`run_scaling_experiment_2.py` was calling `torchrun … run_training_4m.py` directly as a subprocess. Subprocess boundaries don't carry Python monkey-patches, so the neural integration in `lib/train_4m.py` (modality registration, trial sampling, presence masking) was completely bypassed. Both arms — control and treatment — should go through `lib/train_4m.py train` so the patch stack is always in effect.

### Changes Applied

**`run_scaling_experiment_2.py`** — two edits:
1. Add `import sys` to imports
2. Replace `launch_training` subprocess command:

```python
# Before
cmd = ["torchrun", "--nproc_per_node=1", "/opt/repo/ml-4m/run_training_4m.py",
       "--config", str(model_cfg_path)]
if test_run:
    cmd.extend(["--device", "cpu", "--dist_backend", "gloo"])

# After
cmd = [
    sys.executable,
    "/opt/repo/4m_training/lib/train_4m.py",
    "train",
    "--config", str(model_cfg_path),
]
if test_run:
    cmd.extend(["--", "--device", "cpu", "--dist_backend", "gloo"])
```

- `sys.executable` matches the same venv as the parent process
- `lib/train_4m.py train` applies the patches then calls `runpy.run_path("run_training_4m.py")` — the DDP env vars (`RANK`, `WORLD_SIZE`, etc.) are already set by `training_env()` so `os.environ.setdefault(...)` in `run_train` is a no-op
- `--` separator before extra args is stripped by `_clean_extra_argv` and the rest forwarded to `run_training_4m.py`

**`modal_image.py`** — one edit to `training_env()`:
```python
# Added / changed
"PYTHONPATH": f"{REPO}/4m_training/lib:{REPO}/4m_training:{REPO}/ml-4m",
"FOURM_ML4M_DIR": f"{REPO}/ml-4m",
```

- `FOURM_ML4M_DIR` is read by `repo_paths.py` as the first resolution step; without it `repo_paths.ML4M_DIR` falls through to `/opt/repo/external/ml-4m` (doesn't exist on Modal → `FileNotFoundError`)
- Added `4m_training/lib` to `PYTHONPATH` so subprocess-launched `lib/` modules are importable without relying solely on the in-file `sys.path.insert`
- These values propagate transitively: `modal_train.py` → subprocess `run_scaling_experiment_2.py` → subprocess `lib/train_4m.py` (via `os.environ.copy()` at each level)

### To Start a Test Run on Modal
```bash
modal run 4m_training/modal_train.py --dryrun
```
This calls `dryrun_job.remote()` → `_run_train(dryrun=True)` → `run_scaling_experiment_2.py --mode sweep --test_run` → `lib/train_4m.py train --config … -- --device cpu --dist_backend gloo`. The test run uses epoch_size=1024 and total_tokens=0.00001B, so it completes in seconds (CPU, no GPU).

{
  "plan": "# Plan: Neural 4M Scaling Experiment Review\n\n## Context\nUser is running a class project comparing scaling laws for two any-to-any 4M models: a control (RGB↔depth) and a treatment arm (RGB↔depth↔neural recordings). ~300K images, 10% with paired THINGS neural data. $175 Modal budget. Three questions: (1) is the scaling design sound, (2) can validation data use WDS format, (3) are there bugs in the run/config files?\n\n---\n\n## Task 1: Scaling Design Evaluation\n\n### Model Sizes\nThe four registered models span:\n| Config | dim | layers | Est. params |\n|--------|-----|--------|-------------|\n| `fm_neural_2e_2d_gelu_128_dim` | 128 | 2e+2d | ~7M |\n| `fm_neural_2e_2d_gelu_192_dim` | 192 | 2e+2d | ~11M |\n| `fm_neural_3e_3d_gelu_256_dim` | 256 | 3e+3d | ~17M |\n| `fm_neural_3e_3d_gelu_512_dim` | 512 | 3e+3d | ~44M |\n\n~6× param spread is borderline for scaling laws but acceptable for a class project. One caveat: the two small models use 2-layer architectures and the two large models use 3-layer, so depth is confounded with width. Note this as a limitation.\n\n### Token Budget & Data Repetition\n- epoch_size=300,000, tokens/sample=512 → ~153.6M tokens/epoch → **33 epochs** to see 5B tokens\n- Each unique image seen ~33 times. With random masking, crop augmentation, and token sampling this is much less severe than pure memorization, but regularization is limited. For a noticeable trend this is fine.\n- 3 intermediate evals (indices ≈11, 22, 32) give ~1.7B / 3.4B / 5B token checkpoints, all above the 1B filter → **12 (N,D,loss) data points** per condition for Chinchilla fitting. Good.\n\n### Budget Estimate\n- Single A100 @ ~$3.50/hr\n- Rough step time: ~10ms (7M model) to ~40ms (44M model)  \n- Steps per run: 5e9 / (64×512) ≈ 152,600 steps\n- Wall time: ~0.4 hr (tiny) to ~1.7 hr (largest) → ~4.5 hrs per condition × 2 conditions = **~9 GPU hours ≈ $32**\n- Well within $175. Budget is comfortable; even doubling estimates leaves headroom.\n\n### Recommendations\n- **GPU**: Keep A100. It's the right call—smaller GPUs (L4/A10G) save ~30% cost but risk OOM at larger batch sizes.\n- **Batch size**: Consider increasing from 64 → 128 to halve GPU hours. The `blr` already scales linearly with batch size in `run_training_4m.py` (`lr = blr * batch_size / 256`), so `blr: 0.0001` stays correct for either.\n- **Run order**: Run the largest model first to validate the full pipeline before committing all budget.\n- **`save_ckpt_freq`**: Already set to 2, meaning checkpoints every 2 epochs. Fine for result collection.\n- **Fitting**: Chinchilla needs ≥3 points; 12 points is healthy. The mixed-depth design (2e2d vs 3e3d) adds noise to the alpha/beta fit but won't prevent a visible trend.\n\n---\n\n## Task 2: Validation Data in WDS Format\n\n**Short answer: just untar. ## Approved Plan (edited by user):
# Plan: Neural 4M Scaling Experiment Review

## Context
User is running a class project comparing scaling laws for two any-to-any 4M models: a control (RGB↔depth) and a treatment arm (RGB↔depth↔neural recordings). ~300K images, 10% with paired THINGS neural data. $175 Modal budget. Three questions: (1) is the scaling design sound, (2) can validation data use WDS format, (3) are there bugs in the run/config files?

---

## Task 1: Scaling Design Evaluation

### Model Sizes
The four registered models span:
| Config | dim | layers | Est. params |
|--------|-----|--------|-------------|
| `fm_neural_2e_2d_gelu_128_dim` | 128 | 2e+2d | ~7M |
| `fm_neural_2e_2d_gelu_192_dim` | 192 | 2e+2d | ~11M |
| `fm_neural_3e_3d_gelu_256_dim` | 256 | 3e+3d | ~17M |
| `fm_neural_3e_3d_gelu_512_dim` | 512 | 3e+3d | ~44M |

~6× param spread is borderline for scaling laws but acceptable for a class project. One caveat: the two small models use 2-layer architectures and the two large models use 3-layer, so depth is confounded with width. Note this as a limitation.

### Token Budget & Data Repetition
- epoch_size=300,000, tokens/sample=512 → ~153.6M tokens/epoch → **33 epochs** to see 5B tokens
- Each unique image seen ~33 times. With random masking, crop augmentation, and token sampling this is much less severe than pure memorization, but regularization is limited. For a noticeable trend this is fine.
- 3 intermediate evals (indices ≈11, 22, 32) give ~1.7B / 3.4B / 5B token checkpoints, all above the 1B filter → **12 (N,D,loss) data points** per condition for Chinchilla fitting. Good.

### Budget Estimate
- Single A100 @ ~$3.50/hr
- Rough step time: ~10ms (7M model) to ~40ms (44M model)  
- Steps per run: 5e9 / (64×512) ≈ 152,600 steps
- Wall time: ~0.4 hr (tiny) to ~1.7 hr (largest) → ~4.5 hrs per condition × 2 conditions = **~9 GPU hours ≈ $32**
- Well within $175. Budget is comfortable; even doubling estimates leaves headroom.

### Recommendations
- **GPU**: Keep A100. It's the right call—smaller GPUs (L4/A10G) save ~30% cost but risk OOM at larger batch sizes.
- **Batch size**: Consider increasing from 64 → 128 to halve GPU hours. The `blr` already scales linearly with batch size in `run_training_4m.py` (`lr = blr * batch_size / 256`), so `blr: 0.0001` stays correct for either.
- **Run order**: Run the largest model first to validate the full pipeline before committing all budget.
- **`save_ckpt_freq`**: Already set to 2, meaning checkpoints every 2 epochs. Fine for result collection.
- **Fitting**: Chinchilla needs ≥3 points; 12 points is healthy. The mixed-depth design (2e2d vs 3e3d) adds noise to the alpha/beta fit but won't prevent a visible trend.

---

## Task 2: Validation Data in WDS Format

**Short answer: just untar. Don't modify 4M.**

`get_val_dataloader` in `fourm/data/pretrain_utils.py:195` always calls `build_fm_pretraining_dataset` (line 240) regardless of the `use_wds` field—it's silently ignored for val. This calls `MultiModalDatasetFolder` which expects an **ImageFolder-style directory structure** per modality:

```
/project/data/val/cc12m/
  tok_rgb@224/
    samples/          ← one class folder (any name works)
      000000.npy
      000001.npy
      ...
  tok_depth@224/
    samples/
      000000.npy
      ...
  crop_settings/
    samples/
      000000.json
      ...
```

WDS tars extract to flat files like `000000.tok_rgb@224.npy`. A short Python reorganization script handles the conversion:
```python
import tarfile, shutil, os
from pathlib import Path

val_root = Path("/project/data/val/cc12m")
for tar_path in sorted(Path("/project/data/train/cc12m").glob("shard-*.tar")):
    # (pick only your designated val shards)
    with tarfile.open(tar_path) as tar:
        tar.extractall("/tmp/wds_extracted")

for f in Path("/tmp/wds_extracted").iterdir():
    # filename: "000000.tok_rgb@224.npy"
    parts = f.name.split(".", 1)
    modality = parts[1].rsplit(".", 1)[0]   # "tok_rgb@224"
    dest = val_root / modality / "samples" / f.name
    dest.parent.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
    shutil.move(str(f), dest)
```

Run this once per val shard set; no code changes needed.

## Task 3: Bugs

### A. `run_scaling_experiment_2.py`

**Bug 1 (Critical): Wrong path for 3-layer base config** — `line 70`
```python

# CORRECT
BASE_MODEL_CFG_3_LAYERS = "/opt/repo/ml-4m/cfgs/neural/4m/modal/model/4m-neural-3e-3d-scaling.yaml"
```
This causes a `FileNotFoundError` for dim=512 and dim=256 runs.

**Bug 2 (Critical): `extract_model_size` double-appends `/test_run`** — `lines 265-266, 239`
`collect_results` already does `run_dir = run_dir / "test_run"` when `test_run=True`, then passes this modified `run_dir` to `extract_model_size`, which appends `/test_run` again. Fix: remove lines 238-239 from `extract_model_size`.

**Bug 3 (Critical): Wrong args to `run_fit` in "all" mode** — `line 551`
```python
# WRONG
run_fit(RESULTS_FILE, test_run, loss_type)
# CORRECT
run_fit(RESULTS_FILE, SWEEP_OUTPUT_DIR, CONDITION, test_run, loss_type)
```

**Bug 4 (Critical): Wrong args to `plot_results` in `run_fit`** — `line 523`
```python
# WRONG
plot_results(results, law, loss_type)
# CORRECT — also need to thread model_configs through run_fit
plot_results(results, sweep_output_dir, MODEL_CONFIGS, condition, law, loss_type)
```
Add `model_configs=MODEL_CONFIGS` as a parameter to `run_fit`, or reference the global directly.

**Bug 5 (Critical): Wrong result field names in `plot_results` right-axis** — `lines 455-460`
```python
# WRONG

# CORRECT (keys come from collect_results)
pts = [(r["N"], r[f"loss_{loss_type}"]) for r in results if ...]
```

**Bug 6 (Silent): `--test_run` bool parsing** — `lines 537-540`
`parser.add_argument("--test_run", default=False)` with no type means `--test_run False` stores the string `"False"`, which is truthy. Modal passes `"--test_run", "True"` — works by accident but `"--test_run", "False"` would not disable test mode.
Fix: `parser.add_argument("--test_run", action="store_true", default=False)` and remove `"--test_run", "True"` from `modal_train.py` (or conditionally add it).

**Bug 7 (Harmless): `BASE_DATA_CFG` uses underscore** — `line 72`
`rgb_depth-a0.5.yaml` should be `rgb-depth-a0.5.yaml`. This variable is never used in the code, so no runtime impact.

### B. Data Config (`rgb-depth-a0.5.yaml` and `rgb-depth-a0.5-tiny.yaml`)

**Bug 8 (Silent, significant): `weights: [1.0]` for 2 datasets** — last line of train section
`MixtureDataset.__iter__` (unified_datasets.py:537) does `np.random.choice(len(self.sampling_probs), p=...)`. With `weights=[1.0]` and 2 data iterators, it always samples index 0 (cc12m) and **never samples from things**. The THINGS dataset (which contains your neural recording data) is silently ignored.
```yaml
# WRONG
weights: [1.0]
# CORRECT
weights: [1.0, 1.0]
```
Apply to both `rgb-depth-a0.5.yaml` and `rgb-depth-a0.5-tiny.yaml`.

**Bug 9 (Latent): Relative `alphas_config` path for things dataset** — `rgb-depth-a0.5.yaml:49`
```yaml
alphas_config: "cfgs/neural/4m/alphas_mixture/mix_mod7_all2all_rgb2all_a0.5.yaml"
```
When Modal runs from `cwd=/opt/repo`, this resolves to `/opt/repo/cfgs/...` which doesn't exist (should be `/opt/repo/ml-4m/cfgs/...`). Currently masked by Bug 8 (things is never sampled). After fixing Bug 8, this will crash.
Fix: use absolute path `/opt/repo/ml-4m/cfgs/neural/4m/alphas_mixture/mix_mod7_all2all_rgb2all_a0.5.yaml`.

## Route Both Arms Through `lib/train_4m.py`

### Context
`run_scaling_experiment_2.py` was calling `torchrun … run_training_4m.py` directly as a subprocess. Subprocess boundaries don't carry Python monkey-patches, so the neural integration in `lib/train_4m.py` (modality registration, trial sampling, presence masking) was completely bypassed. Both arms — control and treatment — should go through `lib/train_4m.py train` so the patch stack is always in effect.

### Changes Applied

**`run_scaling_experiment_2.py`** — two edits:
1. Add `import sys` to imports
2. Replace `launch_training` subprocess command:

```python
# Before
cmd = ["torchrun", "--nproc_per_node=1", "/opt/repo/ml-4m/run_training_4m.py",
       "--config", str(model_cfg_path)]
if test_run:
    cmd.extend(["--device", "cpu", "--dist_backend", "gloo"])

# After
cmd = [
    sys.executable,
    "/opt/repo/4m_training/lib/train_4m.py",
    "train",
    "--config", str(model_cfg_path),
]
if test_run:
    cmd.extend(["--", "--device", "cpu", "--dist_backend", "gloo"])
```

- `sys.executable` matches the same venv as the parent process
- `lib/train_4m.py train` applies the patches then calls `runpy.run_path("run_training_4m.py")` — the DDP env vars (`RANK`, `WORLD_SIZE`, etc.) are already set by `training_env()` so `os.environ.setdefault(...)` in `run_train` is a no-op
- `--` separator before extra args is stripped by `_clean_extra_argv` and the rest forwarded to `run_training_4m.py`

**`modal_image.py`** — one edit to `training_env()`:
```python
# Added / changed
"PYTHONPATH": f"{REPO}/4m_training/lib:{REPO}/4m_training:{REPO}/ml-4m",
"FOURM_ML4M_DIR": f"{REPO}/ml-4m",
```

- `FOURM_ML4M_DIR` is read by `repo_paths.py` as the first resolution step; without it `repo_paths.ML4M_DIR` falls through to `/opt/repo/external/ml-4m` (doesn't exist on Modal → `FileNotFoundError`)
- Added `4m_training/lib` to `PYTHONPATH` so subprocess-launched `lib/` modules are importable without relying solely on the in-file `sys.path.insert`
- These values propagate transitively: `modal_train.py` → subprocess `run_scaling_experiment_2.py` → subprocess `lib/train_4m.py` (via `os.environ.copy()` at each level)

### To Start a Test Run on Modal
```bash
modal run 4m_training/modal_train.py --dryrun
```
This calls `dryrun_job.remote()` → `_run_train(dryrun=True)` → `run_scaling_experiment_2.py --mode sweep --test_run` → `lib/train_4m.py train --config … -- --device cpu --dist_backend gloo`. The test run uses epoch_size=1024 and total_tokens=0.00001B, so it completes in seconds (CPU, no GPU).

---

## Verification

1. **Smoke test**: `modal run 4m_training/modal_train.py --dryrun` should complete without errors, loading both cc12m and things iterators, and logging modality info for both.
2. **Test sweep**: Run `--mode sweep` with `--test_run` (no argument, using action="store_true") for 1-2 small models; check `train.log` contains "Number of params:" and `checkpoints/log.txt` is populated.
3. **Collect**: Run `--mode collect`; verify `results.json` has entries for all 4 model sizes.
4. **Fit**: Run `--mode fit`; Chinchilla should report fitted params and save plot.

524	class MixtureDataset(IterableDataset):
525	    def __init__(self, data_iters, weights, modality_info):
526	        self.orig_data_iters = data_iters
527	        self.data_iters = [iter(data_iter) for data_iter in data_iters]  # Create initial iterators
528	        self.sampling_probs = np.array(weights) / sum(weights)
529	        self.modality_info = modality_info
530	
531	    def reset_iterator(self, idx):
532	        """ Reset the iterator when exhausted. """
533	        self.data_iters[idx] = iter(self.orig_data_iters[idx])
534	
535	    def __iter__(self):
536	        while True:
537	            dataset_idx = np.random.choice(len(self.sampling_probs), p=self.sampling_probs)
538	            try:
539	                data = next(self.data_iters[dataset_idx])
540	            except StopIteration:  # If the iterator is exhausted
541	                self.reset_iterator(dataset_idx)  # Reset it
542	                data = next(self.data_iters[dataset_idx])
543	
544	            mod_dict = make_empty_mod_dict(self.modality_info)
545	            mod_dict.update(data)
546	            yield mod_dict
547	
548	
549	def build_mixture_dataloader(data_iters, weights, modality_info, batch_size, num_workers, epoch_size, num_gpus):
550	    mixture_pipe = wds.DataPipeline(
551	        MixtureDataset(data_iters, weights, modality_info),
552	        wds.batched(batch_size, collation_fn=default_collate, partial=False),
553	    ).with_epoch(epoch_size // (num_gpus * num_workers * batch_size)) # Pre-define iterator length
554	    
555	    mixture_loader = wds.WebLoader(mixture_pipe, num_workers=num_workers, batch_size=None)
556	    
557	    return mixture_loader

Assistant2026-05-28T02:30:07.423Z
Thinking

Now I have the complete picture. Let me explain the behavior:

  1. epoch_size is purely a pacing/bookkeeping number, not the actual sample count. It controls:
  2. num_training_steps_per_epoch = epoch_size // (batch_size * num_tasks) - how many steps per "epoch"
  3. with_epoch(epoch_size // (num_gpus * num_workers * batch_size)) - how many batches the WDS loader yields per "epoch" (i.e., when it signals StopIteration)

  4. The total epoch count is calculated from the target token budget divided by the tokens processed per epoch

  5. MixtureDataset.__iter__ is an infinite loop (while True: ...). It never stops on its own — it resets exhausted iterators automatically. The "epoch" boundary is entirely imposed by with_epoch(N) which makes the WDS pipeline stop after N batches.

  6. If epoch_size > total_samples: The WDS iterators (ResampledShards) use ResampledShards which by definition resamples with replacement — it's already infinite

. So the shards never truly exhaust; they just cycle through the data multiple times within a single epoch. With wds_n_repeats, shard files are explicitly repeated, so epoch_size can safely exceed the unique sample count without issue.

  1. For the scaling experiment: epoch_size determines how many epochs fit within the fixed total_tokens budget. With epoch_size=300,000, that yields around 33 epochs for a 5B token run, but dropping it to 100,000 (matching the actual cc12m sample count) would stretch that to roughly 97 epochs, fundamentally changing the training duration.

  2. Setting epoch_size to match the full dataset: If I want each epoch to represent one complete pass through all unique samples, I'd set epoch_size equal to the actual dataset size. For cc12m alone, that's roughly 250,000–300,000 samples across 53 shards, but combining cc12m with other datasets complicates the calculation since wds_n_repeats: 2 and equal weighting between sources make it harder to define what "one pass" means precisely.

  3. How epoch_size affects the scaling experiment: Smaller epoch sizes mean more epochs and thus more evaluation checkpoints, generating more (N,D,loss) data points, while larger epoch sizes reduce checkpoint frequency. The 1B token filter already excludes checkpoints below that threshold anyway. The current setup with epoch_size=300,000 and 33 epochs yields three samples around 1.7B, 3.4B, and 5B tokens—all usable. Setting epoch_size to the dataset size gives a clean semantic meaning where each epoch represents a full data pass, but the actual training outcome remains the same for a fixed total token budget since epoch_size only controls checkpoint granularity, not what data gets seen overall.

The LR warmup is controlled by warmup_tokens rather than epochs, so epoch_size doesn't affect that. However, save_ckpt_freq: 2 means checkpoints save every 2 epochs, so larger epoch sizes reduce checkpoint frequency in terms of tokens. To directly address the user's questions: there's no automatic way to compute "use all samples per epoch"—you must explicitly set epoch_size to your dataset size. If epoch_size exceeds total_samples, the WebDataset pipeline handles it gracefully without issues.

Assistant2026-05-28T02:30:17.805Z

Now I have a complete picture. This is straightforward enough to answer directly without more searching.

How epoch_size works

epoch_size is not the number of unique samples in your dataset — it's a pacing number that controls three things:

  1. Steps per epoch: num_training_steps_per_epoch = epoch_size // (batch_size × num_tasks) — how many optimizer steps constitute one "epoch"
  2. WDS iterator length: with_epoch(epoch_size // (num_gpus × num_workers × batch_size)) — when the dataloader signals end-of-epoch to the training loop
  3. Total epochs: ceil(total_tokens × 1e9 / ((num_input_tokens + num_target_tokens) × epoch_size))

The underlying iterator (unified_datasets.py:535-546) is an infinite while True loop that auto-resets any exhausted sub-iterator. ResampledShards is also inherently infinite (samples with replacement). Neither can "run out of samples" — the epoch boundary is purely artificial, imposed by .with_epoch(N).

What happens if epoch_size > total samples

Nothing bad. The pipeline just wraps around mid-epoch. You see some images more than once within a single epoch, which is already happening (you have ~280K images at epoch_size=300,000). The training outcome — total gradient updates, tokens seen, final loss — is identical.

Effect on the scaling experiment

The only effect is eval/checkpoint granularity:

epoch_size epochs to 5B tokens eval checkpoints tokens at 1/3 / 2/3 / final
100,000 (≈ true dataset size) ~97 97 ~1.7B / 3.4B / 5B
300,000 (current) ~33 33 ~1.7B / 3.4B / 5B
1,000,000 ~10 10 ~1.7B / 3.4B / 5B

The 1/3 / 2/3 / final token values barely change because the token filter (total_tokens_seen < 1.0) always gates the 1/3 sample anyway. The scaling law fit is unaffected.

The current epoch_size: 300_000 is fine as-is. If you want epochs to correspond to one pass through all unique images, compute your true sample count and set it explicitly — but it has no effect on the training outcome or your scaling results.

Assistant2026-05-28T02:33:16.225Z

I have enough context from earlier reads. Let me just verify one more thing about the warmup formula.

Both config files have the same training parameters. Here's the full evaluation:

Training Parameter Evaluation

Effective values at runtime (batch_size=64, 1 GPU, bfloat16):

Parameter Config value Computed
blr 0.0001 lr = 0.0001 × 64/256 = 2.5e-5
min_blr 0. min_lr = 0 (decays fully to zero)
warmup_tokens 0.1B warmup_steps = ⌈100M / (512 × 64)⌉ = 3,052 steps
total steps — 5B / (512 × 64) = 152,588
warmup fraction — 2.0%
num_input_tokens 256 —
num_target_tokens 256 —
loss_type mod per-modality average

Warmup assessment: 2% is fine for these model sizes (7–44M). Small models warm up fast and don't need a long ramp. No change needed.

One thing worth checking: min_blr: 0. decays LR all the way to zero. With a cosine schedule over 33 epochs that's aggressive but common. The only risk is that your 1/3-epoch checkpoint (~epoch 11) has LR at ~85% of peak, which is what you want for an intermediate loss sample — this is correct behavior.

Batch size opportunity: Your models are tiny relative to A100 VRAM. At batch_size=64 with bfloat16, the 44M model uses perhaps 500MB of VRAM — out of 40GB. Increasing to batch_size=256 or 512 would cut wall-clock time 4–8× with no change to total tokens trained. The blr scaling rule handles LR automatically (lr = blr × batch_size / 256).

Monitoring GPU Usage in Modal

Modal streams container stdout to your terminal. The simplest approach is a one-liner added to modal_image.py's ensure_fourm() or at the start of _run_train:

# add to _run_train before subprocess.run
subprocess.run(["nvidia-smi", "--query-gpu=name,memory.total,memory.used,utilization.gpu",
                "--format=csv"], check=False)

This prints GPU name, total VRAM, and current utilization at job start, so you see it in Modal logs immediately.

For live monitoring while training is running, Modal's dashboard at modal.com → your app → the running function shows real-time GPU utilization as a chart. You can also SSH into the container if you add modal.enable_memory_snapshot() or use modal shell.

For the batch size tuning loop specifically:

  1. Add this at the top of the first training step in run_training_4m.py — or just watch the Modal dashboard: python # after model.to(device), first forward pass: print(torch.cuda.memory_summary(abbreviated=True))
  2. If utilization is below 60–70%, double batch_size and adjust blr is not needed — the linear scaling is automatic.
  3. Practical target for these model sizes: try batch_size=256 first. At 44M params + bfloat16 + 512 tokens/sample, you should comfortably fit batch_size=512–1024 on an A100-40GB.

One constraint: epoch_size // (batch_size × 1) must stay > 0. At batch_size=512 and epoch_size=300,000 you get 585 steps/epoch — still fine.
